  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dc6b07df-5e82-43fd-a4e9-53ffe271f0dd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer15669207578758104911"><i>She’s searching for answers to her past.   <span id="freeText15669207578758104911" style="display:none"><i>She’s searching for answers to her past. They’re hunting her to save their future.</i><p>World War III has left the world ravaged by nuclear radiation. A lucky few escaped to the Alaskan wilderness. They've survived for the last thirty years by living off the land, being one with nature, and hiding from whoever else might still be out there.</p><p>At least, this is what Juneau has been told her entire life.</p><p>When Juneau returns from a hunting trip to discover that everyone in her clan has vanished, she sets off to find them. Leaving the boundaries of their land for the very first time, she learns something horrifying: There never was a war. Cities were never destroyed. The world is intact. Everything was a lie.</p><p>Now Juneau is adrift in a modern-day world she never knew existed. But while she's trying to find a way to rescue her friends and family, someone else is looking for her. Someone who knows the extraordinary truth about the secrets of her past.</p></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_734511730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/734511730" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/734511730?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=awesome-guy">awesome-guy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer734511730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8915895066871598798"><blockquote>
  <i>Beneath me lies a city. It is not in ruins. It isn’t decimated by war and poisoned by radiation. It is a thriving city with massive glass buildings glistening in the late-afternoon sun. This is not a postapocalyptic wasteland. Where am I? What is going on?</i>
</blockquote>Whoa. WHOA.<br/><br/>I really liked this book---but do take my words with a grain of salt, this is a woman who actually LIKED <i>The Village</i> after all, but the premise of falsehood was revealed to us at the very beginning of the book. This book was so <i>s</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8915895066871598798" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Beneath me lies a city. It is not in ruins. It isn’t decimated by war and poisoned by radiation. It is a thriving city with massive glass buildings glistening in the late-afternoon sun. This is not a postapocalyptic wasteland. Where am I? What is going on?</i>
</blockquote>Whoa. WHOA.<br /><br />I really liked this book---but do take my words with a grain of salt, this is a woman who actually LIKED <i>The Village</i> after all, but the premise of falsehood was revealed to us at the very beginning of the book. This book was so <i>strange</i> at first, and I had no idea what I was reading. I do not go back to the summary of the book once I started, and consequently, the first few chapters had me going "WHAT THE ACTUAL HECK IS GOING ON HERE?"<br /><br />As it turned out, after the beginning disorientation, this book became such a interesting, fun book, with a compelling mystery and characters whom I greatly enjoyed. <b>There is no insta-love. There is a lot of miscommunication. This is fish-out-of-the-water, think Tarzan plopped into the middle of New York City.</b> It was a rollicking adventure, and I enjoyed every step of the way.<br /><br /><u>The Summary</u>: Juneau is a future Sage in her village. It is a tiny community, composed of survivors after the disastrous events of World War III that wiped out all of mankind. It has been 30 years since those events, and her village is entirely self-subsistent. They have to watch out for the remaining survivors of the apocalypse, brigands. They are in close touch with the spirits of nature, they are tapped into the power source of Mother Earth, <b>The Yara</b>. It is a peaceful, quiet life for this band of survivors, as they try to raise their children. The children in her village were all born with starbursts in their eyes.<br /><br />Suddenly, we are in Los Angeles. It is 2014, and Miles is the wealthy son of a pharmaceuticals CEO. He has gotten in trouble for the very last time, and his father is fed up with it. Yale is on the verge of revoking his acceptance, and Miles is desperate for his father to help him regain his admission to his dream college.<br /><br />However will these lives intersect?<br /><br />Juneau returns to her village from a hunt to find it destroyed, razed to the ground. All her loved ones are missing, all remaining is a message from her father. "Juneau, Run!" She sets out to find her father, her friends, her mentor Whit. Juneau consults the Yara, she sees the signs, she knows who to ask. A crazy homeless woman may not be who she seems, anything could carry a message, and Juneau, with her training, knows where to look. The signs tell her to go to Seattle.<br /><br />Miles is working in his father's mail room. He is desperate, bored, seething to get his father's attention and time, to beg him to help him with his admission to Yale. He sees an email in his father's inbox. His father is searching for a missing girl, one with a starburst in her eyes. Bingo. Miles comes up with an exceptionally brilliant plan (to him) to find the girl. She is likely in Seattle. Once he gets to Seattle...the plan doesn't seem so brilliant after all. It is downright dumb.<blockquote>
  <i>But as I walk I begin to get an idea of the scale of the city and start to realize how stupid my plan is. It would be like trying to spot a friend at the Super Bowl without having a clue where their seat is. How in the world am I going to find one girl in the middle of this enormous city? I am well and truly fucked.</i>
</blockquote>It is fate. The Yara knows all, and it draws Juneau and Miles together, improbably. Miles doesn't know what Juneau is capable of, he only knows that he needs to get her back to his father, in order to get back into his graces. His first impression of Juneau is not a good one. <blockquote>
  <i>You’d think she was seeing everything for the first time. Like she’s Tarzan or something—raised by wolves in the deepest, darkest forest. And then there’s the fact that she keeps stopping people and asking their name.</i>
</blockquote>Luckily for Miles, the Yara told Juneau that he is the person she has been waiting for. The one who will help her with her quest to find her family, her mentor, her clan. They join forces, and Miles acts as bewildered chauffeur to a very, very strange girl. There are a lot of trust issues. <b>He thinks she's fucking nuts.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’m lying here in a tent, pretending to be asleep but actually fearing for my life as I watch a bunny murderer have a conversation with our campfire.</i>
</blockquote><b>She thinks he's a fucking moron.</b><blockquote>
  <i>He is likely the stupidest boy I have ever met.<br />He has lived what Dennis would call “a fortunate life, unfortunately for the rest of the world.” The blissfully ignorant spawn of the rich.</i>
</blockquote>These two will have to learn to trust each other, and believe in one another. There is a large barrier separating them, that of credibility. He will have to trust in her abilities. She will have to trust him with her secrets.<blockquote>
  <i>“In 1984, at the outset of World War III, my parents and some friends of theirs escaped from America to settle in the Alaskan wilderness.”<br />“There was no World War III,” I interject.<br />She gives me a frustrated look. “Are you going to listen or what?”<br />I lean back on my elbows and listen.</i>
</blockquote>They will have to find out why Juneau is so valuable to the men pursuing her.<br /><br /><u>The Characters</u>: The characters in this book are so believable. There are major, major trust issues here as Miles struggles to adapt his very modern skepticism to the powers that Juneau supposedly possesses. I believe him. I understand his skepticism. We live in an age where spirituality and powers are dismissed offhand, and I laughed when he is freaking out because this strange, strange girl is talking to the birds, to crazy people, and into a fucking fire. For all he knows, she is insane, and I love seeing his very slow and utterly credible journey into believing in Juneau and trusting in her.<blockquote>
  <i>"Most people I know would have a hard time believing that you weren’t...I don’t know...crazy.”<br />He presses his index finger to his temple and opens his eyes wide. “Or on drugs,” he continues. “Wait, no...I have another theory. You were brainwashed by your hippie cult into thinking you have magical powers. In your head you’re like a cross between...I don’t know...Superpower-Flower-Child and Harry Potter.”</i>
</blockquote>Juneau is not stupid. She is completely, utterly competent. She is brave, she is a fighter, she adjusts. She knows not to trust Miles completely, because he has an ulterior motive. No boy would suddenly obey her every command and follow her off into the wilderness for no reason. He is naive, he may not be trusted, but the Yara pointed him to her, and she has to rely on it, as well as her own instincts.<br /><br /><u>The Romance</u>: <b>Ever so light, and quite believable</b>. Their relationship develops slowly from mistrust to trust, to friendship. I felt like the rush from SHOULD I TRUST HIM/HER into I WANT TO KISS HIM/HER was too fast, but overall, the romance was very well done.<br /><br /><u>My Qualms</u>: There is a spiritual source called the Yara in this book, and while it was well explained, I felt like it was very <i>deus ex machina</i> at points. It solved a lot of problems in the book that might have been completely improbable, at points, like the fact that Juneau and Miles always finds each other, no matter where they are.<br /><br />Overall, my reservations did not greatly decrease my enjoyment of the book, and I liked this book immensely.<br /><br /><u>Quotes were taken from an uncorrected proof and subject to change in the final edition.</u></span>
  <a data-text-id="8915895066871598798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_770825849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770825849" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770825849?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770825849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17277148502875074804">Well... <b>colour me surprised.</b><br/><br/>I don't know what I expected from <i>After the End</i> (though probably not much after reading the reviews of <i>Die for Me</i>) but I definitely didn't expect a book that had me glued to the pages, awake most of the night reading, and laughing out loud on almost every page in the middle section. I had braced myself for "yet another dystopia" and got something more like an entertaining, fast-paced urban fantasy.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Survival. That’s all that’s important. My own survival, and that of </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17277148502875074804" style="display:none">Well... <b>colour me surprised.</b><br><br>I don't know what I expected from <i>After the End</i> (though probably not much after reading the reviews of <i>Die for Me</i>) but I definitely didn't expect a book that had me glued to the pages, awake most of the night reading, and laughing out loud on almost every page in the middle section. I had braced myself for "yet another dystopia" and got something more like an entertaining, fast-paced urban fantasy.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Survival. That’s all that’s important. My own survival, and that of my father and clan. I will do anything to guarantee it. And I will use whoever I need to achieve it.</i>
</blockquote><br>This book starts in the Alaskan wilderness where Juneau has spent her entire life in a small, isolated community. World War III has completely destroyed the world we know and left only this small group of survivors who have managed to stay alive by being at one with nature. Or... that's what Juneau has always been told anyway.<br><br>But one day she returns from a hunt to discover that her clan has completely disappeared. Using the powers of nature that she has been taught, Juneau sets out to find them. However, she soon discovers that there is more to the world than what she's always been told. Finding out that the people she trusted the most have been lying to her is a hard pill to swallow, but Juneau has even bigger problems. The people who kidnapped her clan members are after her and she has no idea why. Chased down everywhere she goes, Juneau is forced to team up with an unlikely companion in order to find her family.<br><br>I have to be honest: I can see straight away why this book won't be to everyone's liking. Almost all of the exhilarating action occurs in the first and last quarters of the book - this is the heart-pounding, ohmigod-how-will-they-get-out-of-this portion of the book. Despite dystopias being forced down our throats left, right and centre, I found this story extremely compelling and I loved how different the two main characters were. But, yes, the biggest chunk of the book in the middle is about a road trip full of bickering, basic survival/camping skills and the development of the relationship between Juneau and Miles.<br><br><u>And I loved it.</u><br><br>I am so not a big romance person. Or at least not in books that are supposed to be action-packed science fiction. But I found the banter between Juneau and Miles truly hilarious. I had to cover my mouth to avoid waking the whole house up with my giggling. They're just such different people. She's a hardcore hunter who's grown up in the wilderness and knows all about survival and taking care of herself... and he's a guy who got kicked out of high school for cheating on an exam. She thinks he's stupid. He thinks she's crazy. <b>Their conversations were a delight to read.</b><br><br><i>“The guys who are following you . . . are they dangerous?” Miles asks finally.<br>“Well, normally I would say that Whit wouldn’t hurt a flea. But from what Poe here told me—”<br>“Poe?” Miles interrupts.<br>“The raven,” I say.<br>“You named the bird?” Miles asks, his voice tinged with a note of hysteria.<br>Yet another reason for him to think I’m crazy, I think, and wonder again if that’s not actually a good thing. “Back in Alaska, we named all our animals after literary figures. It was something our teacher Dennis started, so I was thinking that with Edgar Allan Poe’s poem about the raven—”<br>“Yes, thank you . . . I got the reference!” he snaps. His face is flushed red, but he does this deep-breathing thing and calms down a little. “Okay, first of all, we’re not keeping the bird. So don’t name it. I am not driving you to wherever it is we’re going with a wild animal in my backseat.”<br>“He’s not wild,” I protest.<br>“Has it shit on my shirt yet?” Miles asks, his nose wrinkling like he doesn’t really want to know the answer.</i><br><br><b>I ship them so hard.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399528191ra/9563502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And more than this, I really liked the idea behind the story. No spoilers, of course, but I just thought I'd mention how pleasantly surprised I am to find that I can still fall in love with a dystopian book. For me, this book was incredibly addictive and the characters shone with a rare level of personality. My only real issue was with the ending, which seemed a little abrupt. But, oh well, who cares? <b>I really enjoyed it.</b><br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay" rel="nofollow noopener">Leafmarks</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17277148502875074804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_779251739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779251739" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/779251739?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062225603" href="/book/show/18635064-after-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779251739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4445935523558531816">With an incredibly exciting premise and a unique magical twist, <i>After the End</i> could have swooped me off my feet, but instead I found myself getting increasingly bored as the book went on. What started as a fun adventure involving a girl who finds out that her whole life is based on a lie, ended up being nothing but a dull road trip with flat characters and an artificial romance. <br/><br/>I admit to being compelled at first, however. It begins on a high note when we learn all about Juneau’s way of life as</span>
  <span id="freeText4445935523558531816" style="display:none">With an incredibly exciting premise and a unique magical twist, <i>After the End</i> could have swooped me off my feet, but instead I found myself getting increasingly bored as the book went on. What started as a fun adventure involving a girl who finds out that her whole life is based on a lie, ended up being nothing but a dull road trip with flat characters and an artificial romance. <br><br>I admit to being compelled at first, however. It begins on a high note when we learn all about Juneau’s way of life as a “survivor” after WWIII - or so she thought. Even though it only lasted a few pages, the survivalist lifestyle they had been living was intriguing, and the inclusion of a magical aspect made it all the more fascinating. I enjoyed learning about the Yara and how she could use it to her advantage during her escape. It also had me wondering what eventual twists this story would throw at me. Unfortunately this is where it stopped being fun, or even realistic. <br><br>Juneau soon finds out that there was no WWIII, and the world is actually as it is for us today. She does a double take, takes a night to take it all in, then adapts to it all as if she had not, in fact, been raised in a secluded life away from any kind of civilized modernization. To make matters worse, the dual POV makes us spend time in Miles’ dull perspective while Juneau is off acclimating herself to a new world without us. In a matter of a few pages with Miles, a couple weeks have passed and Juneau is already passing as a regular ol’ homeless teenager. It was a bit too unconvincing. Then, mid-way through the book, this girl who has seen a car for the first time in her life drives one across state by herself like it’s nothing. Right. <br><br>Most of the book consisted of them mindlessly driving from one detour to another, while Juneau droned on about how she was misled and deceived. All without any kind of emotional or psychological depth, of which we merely scratched the surface throughout the whole book. It was just a painfully boring trip. Furthermore, to no one’s surprise, a romance to bloom between the two; a dispassionate and forced romance that felt like nothing more than a plot device to try and lend power to his betrayal and eventual plot developments. On that note, the plot does introduce a few twists that are intriguing, but not especially interesting. Likely due to the lack of character depth and development; I couldn’t have cared less about any of them. <br><br><i>After the End</i> ended up being a drawn-out, tiresome book that lacked the emotional punch it clearly needed. As a result, instead of being entertaining, the plot came off as stale and contrived. Evidently, I was not one with this Yara!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4445935523558531816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1010013027" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1010013027" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010013027?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010013027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4680798351141726482"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430933860i/14780599._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>► <b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283530958' rel='nofollow noopener'>Until The Beginning</a> ★★<br/><br/>When we've been waiting for months to read a book, we can't help but be afraid to feel disappointed in the end. Let's get this straight : You can stop holding your breath, because <b>it wasn't the case here</b>. Indeed while <i>After the end</i> is by no means a flawless book, it delivered almost exactly what I expected : <b>adventure, strong and funny characters, coherent world-building, pretty good writing, and no insta-love</b>. However it lacked something to become a favorite</span>
  <span id="freeText4680798351141726482" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430933860i/14780599._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283530958" rel="nofollow noopener">Until The Beginning</a> ★★<br><br>When we've been waiting for months to read a book, we can't help but be afraid to feel disappointed in the end. Let's get this straight : You can stop holding your breath, because <b>it wasn't the case here</b>. Indeed while <i>After the end</i> is by no means a flawless book, it delivered almost exactly what I expected : <b>adventure, strong and funny characters, coherent world-building, pretty good writing, and no insta-love</b>. However it lacked something to become a favorite of mine, and I'll explain why <s>I'll try, anyway</s>. <br><br>▒ <b>Let's take a look at this graph, shall we?</b> ▒<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430933860i/14780600._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As you can see, I can't say that the plot was <i>always</i> fast-paced, because my interest in the story fluctuated. Indeed, if I wasn't bored in the beginning, I wasn't enthralled either, mostly because I didn't quite understand what the situation was. Now, perhaps it's my fault because... I didn't reread the blurb. Imagine my surprise to switch between Juneau's POV in a post-WW3 world where the world is destructed and the regular teenage life of Miles in high school! See? I was kind of lost there, and I can slap myself for it. Wait - no, actually, no. <b>Because if I got the choice now, I wouldn't change my decision to not reread the blurb or any review before reading it, as the surprise effect was incredible to enjoy</b>. So, people, I won't say too much about the plot either. Just know that Juneau lives in a little community and is able to use Nature's powers in order to get information from her environment. Yes. <i>Magic.</i> As for Miles, well... He is our regular rich teenager who lives in a big city <s>and I'm not saying anything else about him for now, otherwise I'll spend my review rambling about him.</s><br><br><b>Then they meet</b>, and ... Nope, <u>no insta-love, no insta-lust either</u>, only a girl who thinks this city guy is a complete moron and a boy who finds the wild girl batshit crazy. Let's take a moment to savor this. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I turn to him. "Actually, I don't trust you. Frankie told me not to, but he also said I had to be honest with you."<br>"Who the hell is Frankie?" A note of hysteria creeps into Miles's voice. <br>"Frankie is the guy who sits and drinks beer on the corner of Pike and Pine. People call him Crazy Frankie."<br>"You take advice from an insane alcoholic?" (...)<br>"He was my oracle," I respond."</b>
</blockquote><br>I absolutely <b>adored their banter, their misunderstandings, and MILES - OMG. Miles was such a drama queen - fucking HILARIOUS, for real.</b> He's lost, he spends his time freaking out about everything Juneau says or does and doesn't trust her guts one second. But then, how could he react differently? I mean, I did used to camp so the wilderness doesn't scare me but Juneau - Juneau is talking to the fire for fuck sake! And the raven. Oh god, the raven. Let's talk about a weird pet. Therefore as you can guess, the middle part was my favorite by far : I laughed, swooned, was hooked. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I'm lying here in a tent, pretending to be asleep but actually fearing for my life as I watch a bunny murderer have a conversation with our campfire."</b>
</blockquote><br>However, despite the fact that their relationship grows rather slowly - trust issues, guys - I didn't quite felt their physical attraction until the very end. Banter? Yes. Friendship? Yes. Let's kiss? Nope. Not really, and thus I didn't find this particular evolution completely credible - Not at that moment at least. <s>I ship them so hard now</s>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Well, normally I would say that Whit wouldn't hurt a flea. But from what Poe here told me - <br>"Poe?" Miles interrupts.<br>"The raven," I say.<br>"You named the bird?" Miles asks, his voice tinged with a note of hysteria." </b>
</blockquote><br>I didn't reviewed the whole graph, but that's pretty clear, right? <i>Please say yes</i>. <br><br>▒ <b>Now, let's talk about my loves and peeves, okay?</b> ▒ <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430933860i/14780601._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>+++</b> The <b>characters</b>, especially Miles : as I said earlier, in my opinion what makes this book its strength is clearly the way the characters act around each other (except that kiss, okay, I won't go over that again). Between the sarcastic and down-to-earth Miles and the strong-minded and nature connected Juneau, everything leads to fireworks and damn, I loved that something fierce. Moreover, to my delight, <b>both evolve throughout the story</b>.<br><br><b>++</b> The <b>trusts issues</b> were particularly well-handled, as they can't never really know who and what they can believe and trust - <b>and follow their own agenda.</b><br><br>As Serj Tankian would say <s>sing</s>, <br><br>♬ ♪ <i>Lalalalalalalala lie lie lie<br>Lalalalalalalala lie lie lie<br>Lalalalalalalala lie lie lie<br>Lalalalalalalala lie lie lie</i> ♬ ♪<br><br>► You get the general idea. <br><br><b>+</b> I wasn't convinced by <b>the Yara magic</b>, from which I got too many <i>deus ex-machina</i> vibes : even if her powers don't always work, it was frankly way to convenient sometimes, for real. <br><br>In a nutshell, <b>why should you read it?</b><br>✔ Because Miles will make you laugh for sure<br>✔ Because Juneau isn't whiny and fights for what she wants<br>✔ Because the twists toward the end captivated me<br>✔ Because... <i>What? <b>Isn't it enough?</b></i><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4680798351141726482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_931252356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931252356" />
    <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie"><img alt="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505392311p2/11641363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931252356?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie">Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=fantasy-and-magic">fantasy-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931252356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8265330212730702513"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399840421i/9601523.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>So this book was unlike any book I've ever read.</b><br/><br/>Now I don't want to bore people with my thoughts, but that's the whole purpose of reviewing. This book was surprisingly spiritual and philosophical, I know it's a science fiction and a lot of the stuff that happened is "impossible".<br/><br/>I think most people believe or would like to believe that they are part of a higher or divine power, that there is something or someone out there looking out for us. That we aren't just beings alone randomly placed on th</span>
  <span id="freeText8265330212730702513" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399840421i/9601523.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>So this book was unlike any book I've ever read.</b><br><br>Now I don't want to bore people with my thoughts, but that's the whole purpose of reviewing. This book was surprisingly spiritual and philosophical, I know it's a science fiction and a lot of the stuff that happened is "impossible".<br><br>I think most people believe or would like to believe that they are part of a higher or divine power, that there is something or someone out there looking out for us. That we aren't just beings alone randomly placed on this earth by chance. After the End by Amy Plum is that kind of book, it's really just about how powerful believing can be and how debilitating it can be if our entire belief system was taken away. What if everything you believed in was a lie, or what if you had reason to question it. What if your entire existence depends on whether or not you believe.<br><br>Fuck. This is sounding like a church sermon, don't let my review mislead you. Now that I've gotten that off my chest, perhaps I can start my review.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400021404ra/9623846.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>I don't know what I believe anymore. What's right and what's wrong. For me, there are no more rules. I will do anything I need to rescue my clan, no matter who it hurts.</i>
</b><br><br>Let's face it people, we live in a greedy world, everyone wants a piece of the pie or at least a finger in it. Juneau, lives at one with the earth, she and her clan live apart from the rest of the world. The world the elders and her mentor, Whit have told her about is harsh. She returns from a hunt to find her village abandoned, not a person in sight, and she decides to search for her clan. It's in her search that her entire world literally comes crashing down around her. The people she's trusted her entire life are not what they seem and she doesn't know who she can trust.<br><br><b>
  <i>I don't know this place where friends are the bad guys and even this boy sitting next to me can't be trusted. The rules are different. I have faced bears, wolves, snakes, and ice storms. And for the first time in my life, I'm truly scared, I admit.</i>
</b><br><br>So while searching for her clan, she meets Miles, a boy she's supposed to meet. Okay, that makes absolutely no sense so here goes, I'm not a pro at this science fiction stuff. She learns via an oracle that Miles will help her in her search and in rescuing her clan, almost like a prophecy but live.<br><br>So like any good book, there are hurdles along the way which are quickly overcome(this book was sorely lacking in suspense because of this). And a little bit of romance, definitely no insta-love here people. I think many might disagree but seeing as this is a YA novel, I think maybe some of the subject matter was a little heavy, that is if you read between the lines. I can't imagine a 16 year old me taking much away from this book, thing is there's so much more to this book than adventure and science fiction, or whatever you'd like to call it.<br><br>Now on the subject of that bloody cliffy at the end, I can't actually believe that the author would leave us hanging like that! I mean OMG!!! The rationale part of my brain knows how that I probably have absolutely nothing to worry about! But tell that to the irrational part of my brain! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400021404i/9623847.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8265330212730702513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_816882889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816882889" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14066678-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481826762p2/14066678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816882889?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/14066678-christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816882889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8871454751878139439">3.5 stars...I'll bump the rating to 4 because I loved Amy Plums Die For Me series, so I kind of have high hopes for the next one.<br/><br/>The MC, Juneau, was born and raised in the Alaskan wilderness...no electricity, no cars, no stores, no phones. All her life she has been told by her clan's elders that the rest of the world is a post-apocalyptic wasteland, ravaged by nuclear radiation from World War 3. It's been 30 years since the war. Her parents and fifteen others escaped in the very last hours, afte</span>
  <span id="freeText8871454751878139439" style="display:none">3.5 stars...I'll bump the rating to 4 because I loved Amy Plums Die For Me series, so I kind of have high hopes for the next one.<br /><br />The MC, Juneau, was born and raised in the Alaskan wilderness...no electricity, no cars, no stores, no phones. All her life she has been told by her clan's elders that the rest of the world is a post-apocalyptic wasteland, ravaged by nuclear radiation from World War 3. It's been 30 years since the war. Her parents and fifteen others escaped in the very last hours, after the first firestorm of nuclear explosions. They came to Alaska's unspoiled territory, far from any of the major cities that would've been targeted for destruction. They have survived by living off the land, becoming one with nature...As such, they aren't affected by illnesses and don't seem to age past adulthood....All benefits of being as connected as they are to Gaia ( their term for Earth ). They never venture beyond the boundaries of their territory, because they know they're not the only survivors. The elders have seen proof during rare scouting trips of other survivors, who roam the land plundering what is left. <br /><br />That's not all though...Juneau and her clan can also perform " earth magic ". By connecting to the Yara ( a powerful force that connects everything in the Earth. It is the current that moves through all things ) they can connect to other members of Earth's superorganism, reading memory, making predictions, blending with their surroundings, controling the elements and many other things.<br /><br />Juneau returns from a hunting trip to discover that her clan is gone, taken by armed brigands. She's determined to find them and bring them back safely. Leaving the boundaries of their land for the very first time, she makes a horrifying discovery...there never was a war. The world is intact and much more modernized than the one she has been taught about. Everything she has been raised to believe is a lie. <br /><br />But while Juneau looks for a way to rescue her clan, someone else is looking for her...someone who knows the truth about the secrets of her clan's past. <br /><br />This, for me, was a great premise for a book. Pretty original story. And, as mentioned before, I love Amy Plum's writing. But I wasn't quite as fond of this as I was her other series. It was just a bit slow. The world building was fantastic, so no complaints there and I enjoyed Juneau as a MC. Her reactions and emotions were believable and sometimes pretty humorous for the situation she was in. I wasn't all that on board with the romance that developed in the course of this book, I didn't find it all that believable and think just a platonic friendship would've worked better...but that's just my opinion. But overall, it was good. I'll be starting the next one tonight :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8871454751878139439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16466638062380165036">An interesting "post apocalyptic" novel that grabbed my attention from the first page and led me all the way through to a cliff hanger ending (oops sorry if that's a spoiler). I think the "easiness to read" stems from the fact that it is a YA novel, but having said that it is not at all dumbed down.<br/><br/>This book centres on Juneau, the oldest child of a clan living in Alaska following an apocalyptic World War III where a small number of "sensible" adults escaped to set up a colony living off the land</span>
  <span id="freeText16466638062380165036" style="display:none">An interesting "post apocalyptic" novel that grabbed my attention from the first page and led me all the way through to a cliff hanger ending (oops sorry if that's a spoiler). I think the "easiness to read" stems from the fact that it is a YA novel, but having said that it is not at all dumbed down.<br /><br />This book centres on Juneau, the oldest child of a clan living in Alaska following an apocalyptic World War III where a small number of "sensible" adults escaped to set up a colony living off the land in the most natural of conditions. All begins to go wrong when "brigands" attack the clan and all but Juneau are kidnapped.<br /><br />I bought this book for some group read ( that probably occurred months ago, I cannot remember) as I liked the sound of it, and what a good choice that was. Whichever Group it was for, thanks for bringing it to my attention. So much so, that I will certain go on to the sequel, when I've bought it.</span>

<div id="review_1273511132" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273511132" />
    <a title="destini mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia"><img alt="destini mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499903277p2/13742215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273511132?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destini mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destini mia" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia">destini mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273511132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6344274654065701220"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435754857ra/15375080.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>So traitor, you want to play? The game is on.</blockquote>
</i><br/>So, this wasn't what I expected. I don't know what I expected, really. But whatever I <i>would have</i> expected would not have been this. <br/><br/>That sounds kind of bad, but <b>I'm actually pleasantly surprised</b>. The concept of a seemingly post-apocalyptic world with a supernatural twist caught my attention but, like most books I've read lately, I was worried that it would just be "okay". <br/><br/><u>This was not the case</u>.<br/><br/>We have a strong female lead, Juneau, who with Miles m</span>
  <span id="freeText6344274654065701220" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435754857ra/15375080.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <blockquote>So traitor, you want to play? The game is on.</blockquote>
</i><br>So, this wasn't what I expected. I don't know what I expected, really. But whatever I <i>would have</i> expected would not have been this. <br><br>That sounds kind of bad, but <b>I'm actually pleasantly surprised</b>. The concept of a seemingly post-apocalyptic world with a supernatural twist caught my attention but, like most books I've read lately, I was worried that it would just be "okay". <br><br><u>This was not the case</u>.<br><br>We have a strong female lead, Juneau, who with Miles made a hilarious combination. <br><i>
  <blockquote>You have to be tough to survive an apocalypse.</blockquote>
</i> <br>At the tender age of 17, Juneau bears the responsibility of one day have to care for her clan. I was immensely impressed by how seriously she took this role. Everything she did was to benefit her people. <br><i>
  <blockquote>We have a good life, while the world outside our boundaries is nothing but radioactive waste, bands of marauding brigands, and for anyone else who might have survived World War III, an existence filled with misery and despair.</blockquote>
</i><br>Well, she might have been <i>a little</i> off on that. The rest of the world isn't quite marinating in radioactive waste . . . or live in an existence filled with misery and pain. At least not more than you would right now. <br><br><b>Because World War III never happened. </b><br><i>
  <blockquote>Beneath me lies a city. It is not in ruins. It isn't decimated by war and poisoned by radiation. It is a thriving city with massive glass buildings glistening in the late-afternoon sun. People– not dangerous brigands, but normal-looking people– are walking down its street. Cars that look brand-new– more rounded than the ones in the EB– are driving down the roads are parked along their sides. This is not a post apocalyptic wasteland. Where am I? What is going on?</blockquote>
</i><br>How is she going to save her kidnapped clan from an uncertain fate? <br>Well, <b>with the help of Miles</b>. <br><i>
  <blockquote>He is quite likely the stupidest boy I have ever met. </blockquote>
</i><br>What a hilarious pair they made. They are both so different, raised so differently, that they were butting heads all the time. I was have the time of my life watching them attempt to interact with each other. Because no matter how different or how strange they found the other person, <b>they needed each other</b>. <br><i>
  <blockquote>He has lived what Dennis would call "a fortunate life, unfortunately for the rest of the world." The blissfully ignorant spawn of the rich. </blockquote>
</i><br><i>After the End</i> is filled with spirituality, magic, and the supernatural. It was surprisingly philosophical, without getting too heavy. <br><br>Now onto the not so good . . .<br><br>It took me <b>a while</b> to get into this book. I don't know what it was . . . the voice, the beginning . . . <i>something</i> just wasn't letting me connect with the book. To the point where I was ready to put it down and try my luck elsewhere. <br><br>And Miles. I get that he's the neglected but spoiled rich kid with behavioral problems. But I thought his reason for seeking Jeneau out was pretty unbelievable. Like, <i>let me just fly out to wherever this girl is, walk around the city for days until I found someone fitting her description *fingers crossed it's actually her* and then cart her back to my dad and he'll be so impressed with me that I'll earn his good favor back. </i><br><br>Umm . . . ??<br><br>But other than that, I thoroughly enjoyed this book and will be keeping an eye out for book 2.<br><br> <br> <u>Rating: 3.5 stars </u><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"Doubt everything, Juneau. Doubt everything at least once. </blockquote>
</i></span>

    <a title="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit"><img alt="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448295560p2/4163146.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiff at Mostly YA Lit" href="/user/show/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit">Tiff at Mostly YA Lit</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062225603" href="/book/show/18635064-after-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4163146-tiff-at-mostly-ya-lit?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer737681441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8915373565182850206">Review originally posted at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2014/05/after-the-end-amy-plum.html'>http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2014/0...</a><br/><br/>Guys, I was really surprised by this one. 
  <b>It is not what you're going to expect at all.</b>
 I expected it to be sort of like a contemp, a fish out of water story with Juneau integrating into society. Instead, I got a pretty awesome conspiracy thriller with some supernatural/sci-fi elements thrown in. I really liked it.<br/><br/>Here's the story: Juneau is a seventeen-year-old who is happily living with her clan in the wilds of Alaska aft</span>
  <span id="freeText8915373565182850206" style="display:none">Review originally posted at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2014/05/after-the-end-amy-plum.html">http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2014/0...</a><br><br>Guys, I was really surprised by this one. 
  <b>It is not what you're going to expect at all.</b>
 I expected it to be sort of like a contemp, a fish out of water story with Juneau integrating into society. Instead, I got a pretty awesome conspiracy thriller with some supernatural/sci-fi elements thrown in. I really liked it.<br><br>Here's the story: Juneau is a seventeen-year-old who is happily living with her clan in the wilds of Alaska after World War III turned the rest of Earth into a nuclear wasteland. Juneau is poised to become the next "sage", or leader of the clan, because she has great skill in connecting to the Yara, which is the lifeforce that connects all beings and elements. But soon after she takes off on a hunting trip, she returns to her camp to find everyone gone, their animals slaughtered. She sets off on a journey to try to find the rest of her clan, and quickly discovers that WWIII never happened, and the world has advanced without her. Worse, she's now being pursued by thugs, and she's not sure why. Meanwhile, Miles Blackwell is trying to get back into his father's good graces - Miles is a rich brat who's gotten into a lot of trouble at school. When he hears that his father is chasing Juneau, he sets off to find her on his own in the hopes of getting his father to help him get into Yale and put things back to normal.<br><br>Ok, so first of all, the characters. The book alternates between first-person narration from Juneau and Miles. Right away, you know that Juneau is going to be pretty kick-butt. She can hunt, she can fish, she can totally live off the land. She's a badass. But what I really liked about her was that she was also 
  <b>wonderfully fleshed-out in the ways that she reacted to the 2014 world</b>
, and how she persevered in spite of feeling manipulated and lied to. She was never once a woe-is-me character, but she did have a lot of reflection time, and I was fascinated by how much she learned about how she wanted to live versus how people live in 2014.<br><br>Miles is slightly less cool than Juneau - he's kind of your typical spoiled rich kid. But he's also a guy with a good heart who's willing to learn and see past his own idiocy to become a better guy. Also, he's pretty funny. I enjoyed his voice through the novel.<br><br>The thing is, even though you don't know THAT much about Miles and Juneau, you really connect with them and their self-discovery. One of the best parts of the novel was how well everything fit together with Miles and Juneau's journeys and the overarching plot. 
  <b>It all weaves together quite beautifully.</b>
<br><br>A big part of that weaving has to do with the supernatural elements in the story. I'm not usually a fan of that stuff (you guys know how I like my contemps!), but <b>
  I really liked the magic elements and manipulation of nature
</b> in this book, because it was well-explained and really seemed to make sense for the book and the world-building. It was also incredibly fundamental to who Juneau was as a person, and it played so nicely into the end of the novel. I don't want to say more than that.<br><br>If I have complaints, they are that 1) the ending was a little rushed, and 2) the romance resolved a little more quickly than I would have liked. 
  <b>Both the ending and the romance were a little too on-point</b>
, a little too much of the author telling you what the characters have realized. Despite that (I know I'm going to be shot for this), I really kind of liked the ending (it's a cliffhanger!). We know there's more and it felt like the natural place for a cliffhanger if you are going to do one.<br><br>After the End is <b>
  a super-fast read
</b> - I got through it in about four hours, and I found the pace to be quick. There were only a few moments when I was like, "Ok, I get the idea of this part, moving on" - and just as I thought that, the switch was flipped and something changed. So yeah, Amy Plum, you totally anticipated my thoughts!<br><br> <br>Bonuses:  <br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <a href="http://media-cache-ak0.pinimg.com/originals/70/b9/f4/70b9f4a03dfe2aa14a37b725c5f86805.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
          <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399917040i/9609578.jpg" height="200" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
        </a>
      
    
    <br>
    
      Source: <a href="http://www.pinterest.com/pin/437904763739430349/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a>
    
    <br>
  
<br><b>
  Smooth, Divergent-like Writing: 
</b>I really liked the writing in After the End - it totally reminded me of Veronica Roth with its simple, strong sentences. But those sentences are also punctuated with gorgeous descriptions that really fit the voices of the characters. The metaphors and similes they used totally suited them. Have some quotes!<br><br>
  <b> "Through the mosquito net I see the dew-kissed world around us turn rosy pink in the blush of daybreak. There was no war. There are no brigands. I remind myself that an apocalyptic world war never happened. But that image is such an integral part of me that this new world seems like the tall tale--a fairy-tale world, wrapped loosely like colorful paper around the burned-out husk of a postwar planet." </b>
<br>
  <br>
 
  <b>"Juneau looks at me inquisitively like she's wondering whether I'm going to cry, but those rivers have dried, and it's only the furrows they carved into my heart that are left."</b>
<br><br> <br>The Final Word:  <br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br>To me, After the End would be great for fans of <a href="http://mostlyyalit.blogspot.ca/2013/09/the-knife-of-never-letting-go-patrick-ness.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Ness' The Knife of Never Letting Go</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128-the-5th-wave?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Rick Yancey's The 5th Wave</a>. It's a fast-paced twist on the usual post-apocalyptic thriller, with great writing and plotting that holds together well. I'll definitely be picking up book two!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8915373565182850206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_312267005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312267005" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312267005?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=surprised-i-didnt-hate">surprised-i-didnt-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=2014-faves">2014-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=fluffy">fluffy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312267005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16642598920046788422">Mind you, this book came from the exact same author who wrote <i>Die for Me</i>, one of the most boring, cliched and uninspired books I've read. So you can imagine how hard to believe that is, given the fact that I had a ton of fun reading this one.<br/><br/>It was all there: intriguing story that kept me wanting to find out more, great chemistry between the two main characters, and the characters themselves never made me wanna facepalm. Granted, I was pretty bugged by Miles for the first half of the book, since</span>
  <span id="freeText16642598920046788422" style="display:none">Mind you, this book came from the exact same author who wrote <i>Die for Me</i>, one of the most boring, cliched and uninspired books I've read. So you can imagine how hard to believe that is, given the fact that I had a ton of fun reading this one.<br /><br />It was all there: intriguing story that kept me wanting to find out more, great chemistry between the two main characters, and the characters themselves never made me wanna facepalm. Granted, I was pretty bugged by Miles for the first half of the book, since his chapters seemed like they were just....there. And he had this overwhelmingly teenage-boy attitude that annoyed me to no end. But I think the author intended for him to be that way, and it just made his interactions with Juneau all the more hilarious.<br /><br />There was no insta-love by any means here. Sure, there were moments with that whole electric touch trope, but I've said it a million times before that, in YA, you can never escape that. It's just something you have to learn to deal with, which I have. Overall I found Juneau and Miles' relationship to be cute, and the fact that their chemistry was so likable never made the book drag for me, despite the fact that the story was moving quite slow at times. I never got bored, because there was so much to like.<br /><br />Only gripe I have is that ending, which doesn't deserve to be called an ending. The book just ends, mid-scene. I get that the author wanted to have a cliffhanger, but I feel like it should have been at least <i>one</i> chapter longer. Regardless, I guess Amy Plum did it so that the readers would be wanting more, and I suppose she got the job done. Still, even without the cliffhanger, I definitely would have still wanted more anyway.<br /><br />A pleasant, pleasant surprise, this book is. I suppose some authors <i>can</i> improve overtime.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16642598920046788422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_848742297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848742297" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/848742297?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062225603" href="/book/show/18635064-after-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=good-characters">good-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=decent-female-leads">decent-female-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=meh-romance">meh-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=e-arcs">e-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=totally-worth-it">totally-worth-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=sci-fic">sci-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer848742297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15995696350533744466"><i>***This review has also been posted on <b><a href='http://wp.me/p3p0qg-zE' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Social Potato</a></b></i><br/><br/><b> Actual Rating 3.5</b><br/><br/><strong>I am genuinely surprised by how much I liked this one.</strong> I went into <em>After the End</em> expecting to be disappointed, but Khanh’s review offered a glimpse of hope, that perhaps this book wouldn’t be another disappointment. I had even more reason to be skeptical about this one because I haven’t had much luck with dystopias lately and I kind of expected it to be another generic one. Except it wasn’t. <strong>It put a very original spin on </strong></span>
  <span id="freeText15995696350533744466" style="display:none"><i>***This review has also been posted on <b><a href="http://wp.me/p3p0qg-zE" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a></b></i><br /><br /><b> Actual Rating 3.5</b><br /><br /><strong>I am genuinely surprised by how much I liked this one.</strong> I went into <em>After the End</em> expecting to be disappointed, but Khanh’s review offered a glimpse of hope, that perhaps this book wouldn’t be another disappointment. I had even more reason to be skeptical about this one because I haven’t had much luck with dystopias lately and I kind of expected it to be another generic one. Except it wasn’t. <strong>It put a very original spin on the idea of a dystopic world</strong>. Dystopias are so much more than mass destruction and scheming governments. There is so much more to them than just that and <em>After the End</em> realizes that. This was one of the reasons why I was also able to overlook some of the things that bothered me and just sit back and enjoy the novel.<br /><br />The first 1/3rd or so of the novel is not very believable. There seems to be quite a few convenient situations that did initially annoy me and make me wonder how much worse the book could get, but once you get past them, the book starts moving along better and random coincidences start ‘minimizing’.<br /><br />Juneau is going to be the next sage of her tribe and ever since she came into her powers, she has been practicing to defend and protect her tribal members. But then her tribe disappears. After a hunt, she comes back to find all their animals killed and all the members of her tribe gone. So she sets out into the ruins to save them but imagine her surprise when <strong>she learns that everything she has been told has been a lie all along.</strong> There was no World War III that demolished the entire world and lives have carried on for the past 30 years without them.<br /><br />I found Juneau, for the most part, to be a <strong>very likeable female lead</strong>. I understood her naivety, seeing that the world which she was thrust into was so completely different from her own. <strong>I admired her determination and I loved her struggle.</strong> I loved that she was confused and conflicted. These people had lied to her for her whole life but at the same time they were her tribe, her responsibility. She was determined to save them but at the same time she lost faith in everything they had taught her and had to rebuild her belief system.<br /><br />Miles on the other hand, yeah. <strong>He was a confusing one</strong>. I never understood his determination to help Juneau and his voice just didn’t work for me. He seemed more like a pre-teen than an 18 year old. <strong>He was stubborn, spoiled, and usually didn’t think twice before doing something</strong>. He was <strong>very impulsive</strong> and kind of contradicted Juneau. That did seem to be intentional but the contradiction didn’t have the effect it could have had if Miles hadn’t been so pig-headed all the times.<br /><br />One of my favorite secondary characters (or I should say the only notable one) was Tallie.<br /><blockquote>
  <strong>“Doubt everything, Juneau. Doubt everything at least once. What you decide to keep, you’ll be able to be confident of. And what you decide to ditch, you will replace with what your instincts tell you is true.”</strong>
</blockquote><br />She gave the best advice and helped Juneau recover faith in things that were important to her, but she also gave her room to doubt things. I found Tallie’s appearance to be random and not as well planned out as it could have been, but the heart of the purpose her character served somehow worked in spite of the flaws surrounding their meeting.<br /><br /><strong>The romance, predictably, wasn’t all that great either</strong>. At first it wasn’t based on insta-attraction. Neither liked the other very much but they had to rely on one another which consequently built an odd bond of sorts. But then the romance jumped out of nowhere. They kissed and I was just sitting there wondering what the hell had happened and where the kiss had come from.<br /><br /><strong>The plot, although not particularly strong, was incredibly enjoyable.</strong> Kids on the run helps. Always. It usually makes for <strong>an exhilarating and exciting read</strong> and as someone who enjoys a good adventure/survival story, I didn't feel differently about this book in terms of that. The ride was a little bumpy (those bothersome conveniences I mentioned) but aside from that it was fun and it didn’t take me much time to devour the book.<br /><br /><strong>I also enjoyed the concept of Yara</strong>. It’s not particularly original but the way it was presented was awesome. I am quite looking forward to see what the future installments hold in store for us.<br /><br />Like I mentioned before, my biggest problem with this book was the random conveniences. Here was this girl who was carrying more money than anyone should be and no one really did anything about it. They might fleetingly mention it but for the most part it almost seemed like it was a normal occurrence. On top of that, if the money had come from an illegal source, the people who took money from her could get into big trouble which was why I was surprised when no one really said anything. Also there was that part where Miles reads his Dad’s email. His father apparently didn't have a password on his computer. He was a CEO and didn't have a password on his home computer. Does anyone else see what is wrong with that?<br /><br />Also the cliffhanger. Nope. Not happy. Why would anyone do that? End on such an extreme note. That’s not a very nice thing to do.<br /><br /><strong>This book, on the whole, is quite enjoyable</strong> but one’s ability to enjoy it will depend on whether you could overlook some grievances in order to enjoy the overall ride. I could and I ended up enjoying it. I would definitely recommend it to someone like me who is getting tired of generic dystopias and wants something new and (relatively) unique to look forward to.<br /><br /><i>Note that all quotes have been taken from an uncorrected proof and may be subject to change</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15995696350533744466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
