  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774500913" />
    <a title="Lucia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia"><img alt="Lucia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484242793p2/8837962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/774500913?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucia" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia">Lucia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer774500913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16218015494349338981">My Juneau and Miles:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390207665i/8165376.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>17-years old gifted girl hiding from aftermaths of nuclear war and determined to do anything to protect her clan, suddenly finds out that her whole life was a fabricated lie. A spoiled boy who is used to always geetting his way and now he wants to prove himself to his dad. Can these two fundamentally different people help each other to reach their goals?</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390207665i/8165377.png' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I liked that main protagonists were from completely different backgrounds. Once they were together (not in romantic kind of </span>
  <span id="freeText16218015494349338981" style="display:none">My Juneau and Miles:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390207665i/8165376.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>17-years old gifted girl hiding from aftermaths of nuclear war and determined to do anything to protect her clan, suddenly finds out that her whole life was a fabricated lie. A spoiled boy who is used to always geetting his way and now he wants to prove himself to his dad. Can these two fundamentally different people help each other to reach their goals?</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390207665i/8165377.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked that main protagonists were from completely different backgrounds. Once they were together (not in romantic kind of way), story caught spark and got interesting. It was fun watching nature-oriented girl who has no idea about modern world interact with spoiled "blissfully ignorant" rich boy. <b>Paired together, Juneau and Miles were great and entertaining!</b> But as individual characters, they were not strong or interesting enough. And that was exactly my biggest problem with this book. I lacked real connection with narrators (dual POV) and their character growth felt unnatural and too abrupt most of the time.<br><br>Moreover, I was slightly overwhelmed with all those new information and Juneau's skills coming out of nowhere through out the whole book. There were no hints and new revelations were popping out of nowhere when it was needed and <b>it felt too convenient</b>... It seemed like author made things up along the way without thinking it through before and it just didn't work for me. <br><br>As you can see, I am a little bit torn when it comes to this book. It wasn't bad, I definitely don't regret reading it because I liked some of the original ideas presented in this book. But I never loved it and missed a good angst since most of the problems were resolved pretty quickly and easily. This series definitely has some potential and I will probably check next book when it comes out to see where is author taking this story.<br><br>And just a little warning at the end. I know that authors have no power over the way books are being shelved here on Goodreads BUT this book is definitely doesn't belong within dystopian/post-apocalyptic genre. It is mostly <b>fantasy/supernatural</b> story. Just so you know :)<br><br><i>*ARC provided by publisher as an exchange for honest review*</i><br><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Reading Is My Breathing</b>

<div id="review_891619541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/891619541" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/891619541?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cliffhanger-ending">cliffhanger-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=harper-teen">harper-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer891619541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7611913606169400186">Although I’m a big fan of Amy Plum’s Revenants series, I started After the End with no small amount of trepidation. Writers are sometimes more than just defined by their first story, they get stuck writing endless variations of it, unable to find their voice elsewhere. For whatever reason, I feared that Plum might be one of those authors. Boy, was I ever wrong.<br/><br/>I’ve had little time to read and even less patience for it lately, being preoccupied with finishing my thesis in time. Therefore, finding</span>
  <span id="freeText7611913606169400186" style="display:none">Although I’m a big fan of Amy Plum’s Revenants series, I started After the End with no small amount of trepidation. Writers are sometimes more than just defined by their first story, they get stuck writing endless variations of it, unable to find their voice elsewhere. For whatever reason, I feared that Plum might be one of those authors. Boy, was I ever wrong.<br><br>I’ve had little time to read and even less patience for it lately, being preoccupied with finishing my thesis in time. Therefore, finding something to read that would make me drop everything else and focus on it entirely proved to be incredibly hard. And yet, I started After the End at 9 pm, and finished it that very same night.<br><br>The idea of someone’s life being built entirely on lies fascinated me to no end. Juneau was raised believing that World War III ended the world as we know it in 1984, leaving just a few survivors scattered around the planet. Her small clan supposedly found salvation in Alaskan wilderness, far away from civilization and technology. Through their close connection with nature, they developed certain powers that others would love to exploit. And Juneau, being the most powerful among them, is the most important father.<br><br>As the son of a pharmaceutical mogul, Miles is your typical attention-seeking spoiled rich kid. In trying to get back in his father’s good graces, he sets out to find the one person his father wants above all else – a young girl with very strange eyes. <br><br>These two are so interesting together. It’s clear from the start that they couldn’t be more different. Miles was raised with access to all the commodities of the 21st century, and Juneau with a clear understanding of the world beneath. The animosity they felt towards each other and the level of mistrust were expected. No starry eyes for those two! I felt that the progression of their relationship was handled beautifully, with deliberate slowness and tact. When you add to that their hilarious banter, it’s clear why they quickly became one of my favorite couples. <br><br>This world and these characters have a lot more to give, and while I don’t appreciate or even understand cliffhangers, I was left with just enough hope to tide me over until the next book. That said, hurry up, Ms. Plum! I realize living in Paris can be distracting, but would you please write faster?!<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_324760279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/324760279" />
    <a title="Mel (Daily Prophecy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy"><img alt="Mel (Daily Prophecy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599044849p2/5387491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/324760279?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel (Daily Prophecy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel (Daily Prophecy)" href="/user/show/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy">Mel (Daily Prophecy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy?shelf=disappointing-af">disappointing-af</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy?shelf=physical-review-copy">physical-review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy?shelf=incoming-2014">incoming-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5387491-mel-daily-prophecy?shelf=gave-away">gave-away</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer324760279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13025865502883564255"><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://thedailyprophecy.blogspot.nl/2014/05/review-259-amy-plum-after-end.html'>http://thedailyprophecy.blogspot.nl/2...</a><br/><br/>I am left frustrated and confused by this book. I liked the idea of a community in Alaska after World War III; the only thing is, Juneau finds out this never happened. I thought it would give some interesting situations, with Juneau trying to blend into the modern world and her mission to save her clan. Instead, I was bored and it seemed to take me a lot of time to finish it. The slow pacing doesn’t work here. I am familiar with her other series so I know </span>
  <span id="freeText13025865502883564255" style="display:none"><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thedailyprophecy.blogspot.nl/2014/05/review-259-amy-plum-after-end.html">http://thedailyprophecy.blogspot.nl/2...</a><br /><br />I am left frustrated and confused by this book. I liked the idea of a community in Alaska after World War III; the only thing is, Juneau finds out this never happened. I thought it would give some interesting situations, with Juneau trying to blend into the modern world and her mission to save her clan. Instead, I was bored and it seemed to take me a lot of time to finish it. The slow pacing doesn’t work here. I am familiar with her other series so I know she likes her cliff-hangers, but this ending felt too abrupt.<br /><br />Juneau grew up with the knowledge she was going to be the next clan leader. She is capable of ‘Reading’ which is done with the energy from Yara. Whit is her guide, but everything he ever told her appears to be a lie. When Juneau returns from hunting, her clan is kidnapped and people are looking for her. She runs into Miles, which is just such a stupid coincidence. He is looking for her, because his father is after her and Miles hopes to get some credits. This leads to a lot of the same: traveling, escaping and running. <br /><br />I disliked how Miles is able to find Juneau that easily. She changed her looks, so there is no way he could recognize her after that transformation. It was something that happened to make the story unravel, but it was by no means realistic. Also, Juneau grew up in isolation, but she is able to drive a car without any problem? <br /><br />Juneau and Miles obviously don’t trust each other, but they are aware they need each other at the same time. Miles is “the blissfully ignorant spawn of the rich” and Juneau is a “paranoid schizophrenic.” It’s not long before they start to get feelings, even when Juneau had some clever moments where she tells herself that there is no time for a stupid teenage boy. But, like many other weak Dystopian MC’s, she soon falls for his charm. <br /><br />I feel okay about both characters. They aren’t the best, but I've encountered worse characters. I felt a little disconnected from them and the interesting plot around Juneau’s reading powers doesn’t get to shine. The slow pace kills everything and that is a shame. Most annoying about this book? The fact that the ending makes me want to read the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13025865502883564255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7996561298914860140" style="display:none">I really don't know what is happening on the first few chapters of this book since what I have read was really confusing to the point that everything doesn't make sense. But goodness gracious I was so happy that I didn't drop reading this book because (oh gods) after those confusing first few chapters, After the End, in my opinion, was great, compelling and a fun read.<br /><br />I may not remember everything about this book but I can't forget how I really loved this one-- from the interesting plot, well-paced story line to the likable and awesome main characters (Juneau and Miles). Even the romance worked well for me. It isn't annoying and overdone or even insta-love. I think the author really crafted it well that the friendship/love between the two main characters has been adored by the likes of me. (Or maybe it is just me).<br /><br />I am so excited for the sequel. True? True.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6354257418658013365">This started off with a bang, and then it fizzled out for me. I thought I was going to be reading about the baddies who went through all this trouble to segregate a small group of people and then find out they had sinister goals. Well THAT was there, but it wasn't the main focus. I honestly thought it was a romance novel with a post-apocalyptic setting. Thought it was unnecessary and wasn't too vital with the entire plot. Then there was the fact that this adventure or journey or whatever you wan</span>
  <span id="freeText6354257418658013365" style="display:none">This started off with a bang, and then it fizzled out for me. I thought I was going to be reading about the baddies who went through all this trouble to segregate a small group of people and then find out they had sinister goals. Well THAT was there, but it wasn't the main focus. I honestly thought it was a romance novel with a post-apocalyptic setting. Thought it was unnecessary and wasn't too vital with the entire plot. Then there was the fact that this adventure or journey or whatever you wanted to call it, was boring. I was waiting for something or anything to happen, but I felt nothing for the characters.<br /><br />I liked the fact that finally, there is a character who is half Chinese and American. That made me drop some diversity points along the way. Yay for highlighting people of other ethnicities! The simple magical element made it interesting, but it wasn't strong enough for me to even consider reading the rest of the series.<br /><br />Good concept but not a whole lot of movement in the plot points which made me cringe at certain moments. If you're looking for a sci-fi novel, look elsewhere, because I was bored and forced myself to finish this. </span>

<div id="review_1210838103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1210838103?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=superpowers">superpowers</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1210838103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10383987531728600930"><b>*2,9/5 stars*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Life is easier in black and white. It's the ambiguity of a world defined in grays that has stripped me of my confidence and left me powerless.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Pretty promising book. I loved the first half, the second... not so much. It's like, after the intriguing build-up, it all fizzled out in the next half. I wanted more action, more suspense and some shocking revelations. Nothing like that happened. It got a bit flat and dull and I lost interest in reading it more than a few times.<br/>The two </span>
  <span id="freeText10383987531728600930" style="display:none"><b>*2,9/5 stars*</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Life is easier in black and white. It's the ambiguity of a world defined in grays that has stripped me of my confidence and left me powerless.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Pretty promising book. I loved the first half, the second... not so much. It's like, after the intriguing build-up, it all fizzled out in the next half. I wanted more action, more suspense and some shocking revelations. Nothing like that happened. It got a bit flat and dull and I lost interest in reading it more than a few times.<br />The two different and very distinctive points of view were so much fun, especially in the first half, in the second I got a little bored with them. The heroine was likeable enough, but I couldn't really connect with either of the characters. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I'm lying here in a tent, pretending to be asleep but actually fearing for my life as I watch a bunny murderer have a conversation with our campfire.”</b>
</i><br /><br />&lt;-- Miles's fun remarks were one of the highlights of this book.<br /><br /><i>After the End</i> is entertaining book with enough intrigue to keep one reading, though falls flat toward the end and feels a bit anticlimactic. Still, there is some potential and I hope that the next book will be a bit more.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Doubt everything. Doubt everything at least once. What you decide to keep, you'll be able to be confident of. And what you decide to ditch, you will replace with what your instincts tell you is true.”</i>
</b></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099288522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17135028528730386478">3.7 stars- audio<br/>Tricked, betrayed and abandoned Juno a young teenage girl goes looking for her family. She was raised to believe that the end of the world has basically happened and her family was all that was left. While off on a hunting trip her whole life was shaken into another realm. Everything she was taught, everything she believed may have been a lie. She must go out into this foreign world and find the answers, but will the truth be too painful ? She has never known the world she is now</span>
  <span id="freeText17135028528730386478" style="display:none">3.7 stars- audio<br />Tricked, betrayed and abandoned Juno a young teenage girl goes looking for her family. She was raised to believe that the end of the world has basically happened and her family was all that was left. While off on a hunting trip her whole life was shaken into another realm. Everything she was taught, everything she believed may have been a lie. She must go out into this foreign world and find the answers, but will the truth be too painful ? She has never known the world she is now in, and she has to trust an outsider to complete her mission. Both tot them will learn many lessons and loose some of their innocence.<br />Interesting, the raised in another world while really in this world was an interesting concept. She is the special little bee that is all too common is YA books but this little bee has holes in her wings and it is a nice touch. There is a lot of doubts, and thinking, this girl thinks and follows through with her choices. Not all of them are smart, but they are who she is. The reason her people have been taken was a little misty, but leading to what could be a very interesting story. She could be medically improved, spiritually improved or a genetic mutation ? I have my preference and hope it goes my way. The romance, was extremely brief and for me it wasn't right at the moment so I was happy the author backed off. Things had gotten intense, changing, moving and BOOM the book ended. I hate cliffhangers. Now, I need to find out when book 2 comes out</span>
  <a data-text-id="17135028528730386478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_775150130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/775150130" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/775150130?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=serious-cliffhanger">serious-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775150130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16878069252384589205"><b>*4.5 Stars!*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>I am on fire. A golden statue alight, flames licking around me, melting the snow into puddles at my feet, heating Juneau's face and reddening her nose and cheeks. She leans in closer until her lips are touching mine. And as she kisses me I disperse into a million tiny flames, sparks flying up into the cold winter air and diffusing once they hit the starry night sky.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Life, as I've been telling all my lovely GR friends lately, apparently is not a wish granting factory. I've been see</span>
  <span id="freeText16878069252384589205" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars!*</b><br><br><b>
  <i>I am on fire. A golden statue alight, flames licking around me, melting the snow into puddles at my feet, heating Juneau's face and reddening her nose and cheeks. She leans in closer until her lips are touching mine. And as she kisses me I disperse into a million tiny flames, sparks flying up into the cold winter air and diffusing once they hit the starry night sky.</i>
</b><br><br>Life, as I've been telling all my lovely GR friends lately, apparently is not a wish granting factory. I've been seeing that a lot lately and I have been in one of those totally depressed, funky moods where yeah, I'm liking books just fine but, I'm not in the best place about it. So when I looked at my Ipad and was trying to decide which dystopian to tackle (that was-and is-what I was in the mood for) I had three or four loaded and ready to go-I narrowed it down to two, and then ultimately chose this one because I've been excited about it the most for the longest time-and I chose correctly. I had a smile on my face the minute that Miles and Juneau met-and it very rarely left my face throughout the entirety of the novel.<br><br><b>Life is easier in black and white. It's the ambiguity of a world defined in grays that has stripped me of my confidence and left me powerless.</b><br><br>These two are complete polar opposites-you couldn't find a more comical pairing. One lives off the land and is in tune with nature while the other is privileged and pampered and lives in a world where everything has always been handed to him on a silver platter. I loved the dynamics of their relationship and everything in-between. There was no insta-love (GAG) and they were both (knowingly) using each other to get what they needed-it just turns out that they want the exact opposite thing....go figure.<br><br><b>"The guys who are following you...are they dangerous?" Miles asks finally.<br>"Well, normally I would say that Whit wouldn't hurt a flea. But from what Poe here told me-"<br>"Poe?" Miles interrupts.<br>"The raven," I say.<br>"You named the bird?" Miles asks, his voice tinged with a note of hysteria.</b><br><br>I think the biggest reason why I loved this book so much is because it wasn't full on dystopian and <b>it didn't try to be.</b> I love this genre, but sometimes authors try way too hard and it doesn't portray quite what they want to. So, when this didn't turn out to be a cut and dry survival story, I was kind of excited. Basically, Juneau left her clan to go hunt for food-they live secluded and 'protected' from the <b>dystopian like world outside their living site</b> from the after effects of World War III....and when Juneau returns, her dad and the whole clan included have disappeared. She knows she must try to find them immediately with her knowledge of the land and way of Kara (not even going to explain-it's not that complicated but I would still mess it up). But when she leaves the confines of her camp and starts to get farther and farther away from what she's always known, she finds out about the biggest betrayal she never would have imagined-<b>there was no WWIII and she has been living a lie.</b> And what's worse, people are after her-maybe even one of the people she's trusted her entire life.<br><br><b>"Has it shit on my shirt yet?" Miles asks, his nose wrinkling like he doesn't really want to know the answer.<br>"Birds don't shit while they're sitting down. They would be sitting in their excrement, and if you haven't noticed-which of course you haven't, you"-I can't think of an insult that fits the bill-"city boy, birds are clean." I don't know why I'm getting all defensive about Poe, but I can't help correcting Mile's glaring misconception.<br>"Secondly," Miles continues, ignoring my argument, "a little while ago, you confirmed my long-held belief that birds don't talk. Yet you just said that Poe"-he pauses-"I can't believe I just called it that...this bird told you something."<br>"I shouldn't have said 'told.' I should have said 'showed.'"<br>"Because that makes a difference?"</b><br><br>Miles lives a life of debauchery and opulence-he repeatedly causes problems in school and has finally been kicked out-a month before graduation. When he hears his father is looking for a girl who is the key to a drug he wants, Miles knows he is more than capable of finding a girl who knows nothing of the city and is virtually a stranger to the world. All he wants is his father's approval and if he can get it by bringing the girl back in for questioning, he will do anything he can to get that accomplished. But what happens when he meets the girl and travels with her on the journey to find her clan? He starts to get to know her and see what kind of person she is. She's as clueless as he is about the whole thing-what if his father is wrong and is after an innocent girl....what will he do then? And even more than that, what will he do when he starts to fall for this crazy girl who eats innocent wildlife and forages in the woods and is the complete opposite of his personality-what if she's exactly what he's been looking for his whole life: a place where he feels like he belongs. What then?<br><br><b>The touch of our skin sets off a reaction in me. I am immediately awake...100 percent present. And it feels like a whirlwind of thorns is whipping around in my chest, stinging me all over from the inside. That makes it sound painful. It isn't. It's the kind of itching sensation that makes you want to do something crazy. That spurs you forward to act on an idea you didn't even know was in your head.</b><br><br>The dynamic of this story wholly worked for me and there were rarely any parts that bored me. There was information to take in at every twist and turn, but I never felt like I was getting info-dumped. It's hard to find that in stories-that balance where there's just enough cute, sweet, tough, travel, info....peril. It's a delicate process and while I do wish the peril was amped up a bit, I still thought it was wonderfully done and I had hardly a complaint throughout the entire process. <br><br><b>It's not like she's wearing a dress. She just has on a pair of black jeans and a red V-neck shirt. But for once they actually fit. Juneau's not skinny, and you wouldn't exactly say muscular. But something in between. She's so much shorter than me that I could easily pick her up. Of course, I refrain since I don't feel like being punched.</b><br><br>So, all in all, a total win in my book-it takes a lot to make me completely happy, but this book got as close to perfect as I've seen in a while. When I'm in a foul mood it is quite a process to make me smile, much less laugh, so when ATE succeeded in both, I knew I would be sad to see it end. Speaking of which-that end?? Awesooooommmeeeeeee! I can't wait until book two. <br><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews visit<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="240" width="385" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407869528i/10772466._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16878069252384589205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_780362263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/780362263" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/780362263?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=arc-edelweiss">arc-edelweiss</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-mar-2014">zzread-mar-2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer780362263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9061928637825345827"><i>Update 12/25/14</i> <b>After the End</b> was chosen as one of <a href='http://badassbookreviews.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Badass Book Reviews</a> favorite Young Adult/New Adult SciFi/Dystopia books of 2014. Read all about it <a href='http://badassbookreviews.com/badass-best-of-2014-ya-na-speculative-fiction/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/><i>Initial Thoughts:</i> This was really good, about 4.5 stars with .5 stars deducted for ending too soon, lol. The story is told in alternating first person points of view of the main characters Juneau and Miles. Juneau lives in a small enclave near Denali, Alaska. Miles lives a privileged life in LA. At first, I wondered what the two could possibly</span>
  <span id="freeText9061928637825345827" style="display:none"><i>Update 12/25/14</i> <b>After the End</b> was chosen as one of <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews</a> favorite Young Adult/New Adult SciFi/Dystopia books of 2014. Read all about it <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com/badass-best-of-2014-ya-na-speculative-fiction/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br /><i>Initial Thoughts:</i> This was really good, about 4.5 stars with .5 stars deducted for ending too soon, lol. The story is told in alternating first person points of view of the main characters Juneau and Miles. Juneau lives in a small enclave near Denali, Alaska. Miles lives a privileged life in LA. At first, I wondered what the two could possibly have in common. Then they find each other in Seattle and Miles is conscripted to help Juneau find her clan. Oh, and Juneau is very special so the bad guys are chasing them. Wonderfully written, hard to put down. <br /><br /><i>The Review:</i><br />I can't even begin to imagine how I would react if I found out that my whole life was a sham. Personally, I might just curl up into a ball and just check out. Not Juneau, the 17 year old girl at the center of <b>After the End</b>. Juneau is one plucky heroine. She responds by going on a road trip. Let's take a step back - Juneau has lived an isolated existence with her clan in the Denali Forest. When her home (they lived in yurts!) was attacked and her friends and family were kidnapped by marauders (or what appears to be marauders), Juneau vows to find them. Then she discovers that the world is very different from what she thought. <br /><br />Juneau begins to experience a lot of new things - she's never seen a city before, nor has she ever seen so many people. Despite all of her lack of experience, she is remarkably savvy at surviving and even manages to find her way from Anchorage to Seattle by ferry. Juneau remains one step ahead of her pursuers. <br /><br />The story is told in alternating points of view. We get to see the world through Juneau's eyes and at first I really felt like I was reading a totally different story. All the things that we take for granted in our world are new to Juneau. The second point of view is that of Miles Blackwell, the son of the big pharma company that is pursuing Juneau. Miles lives the life of a privileged rich boy and he keeps getting himself into trouble. He believes that if he helps his father find the missing girl, he will gain favor in his father's eyes. When I first started reading, I couldn't see how these two points of view fit together. It really felt like two different stories and two different worlds. <br /><br />This is a fun story where our main characters learn about themselves and begin to question their upbringing. I did enjoy the road trip and how the two learned to work together. There is a mystical aspect to this book and I am looking forward to reading the next installment to see how that pans out. <br /><br /><i>Thank you to Edelweiss and Harper Teen for a review copy of this book. </i></span>

<div id="review_791595347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791595347" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791595347?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791595347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12388811252209504972">This review appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/01/05/after-the-end-by-amy-plum-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br/><br/>As I was warned, After The End isn’t a dystopian but instead, a contemporary/dystopian blend. It features an interesting outlook from a girl who thinks that World War III has happened and that her clan are the only survivors, but finds out she was lied to all along.<br/><br/>Juneau has lived in the Alaskan wilderness all of her life, and when her clan goes missing, she stumbles upon civilization in her search. I could not imagine how </span>
  <span id="freeText12388811252209504972" style="display:none">This review appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/01/05/after-the-end-by-amy-plum-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br /><br />As I was warned, After The End isn’t a dystopian but instead, a contemporary/dystopian blend. It features an interesting outlook from a girl who thinks that World War III has happened and that her clan are the only survivors, but finds out she was lied to all along.<br /><br />Juneau has lived in the Alaskan wilderness all of her life, and when her clan goes missing, she stumbles upon civilization in her search. I could not imagine how incredibly unsettling and traumatic this would be, and Juneau gets accustomed to the new world and technology a bit too quickly and easily. For someone who was brought up in the wilderness, without anyone to teach her what things are, she gets used to the idea of iPhones a bit too easily and doesn’t display signs of trauma or shock. Searching for Sky was a reverse dystopian who did this aspect really well, which influenced my thoughts here.<br /><br /><i>Sorry I tried to impress my dad by finding her. Sorry I’ve been making fun of a brainwashed girl for a delusion she can’t help. Sorry I egged her on just to make my point.</i><br /><br />The other lead character in the book was Miles, whose character I just wasn’t convinced on. I just didn’t know what his intention was; he tracks down Juneau to bring her back to his dad’s organisation, but then he camps out in the woods with her and decides to drive her around. He just thinks Juneau is this weird girl and doesn’t believe everything she says, yet somehow he still ends up having feelings for her. I felt the relationship was quite forced and wasn’t convinced at all, given how close-minded Miles was.<br /><br />I did like the paranormal aspects in the novel though. Juneau has a star on her right pupil and has powers from ‘connecting to the Yara’, a spiritual guide. She can see through people’s eyes in a fire, morph her appearance, even use people as oracles to guide her way. You’ll wonder why she has these powers to begin with, but surprisingly the ending actually gave a valid explanation for everything. I was actually pretty impressed, given my earlier skepticism. It ends on a pretty annoying cliffhanger though.<br /><br />Although After The End had quite a few illogical and unconvincing parts, and a character I was slightly offended at, it still managed to provide an interesting story with an unusual girl. It really made me think how I would react if I was in that situation and what I would do when I found myself alone from everything I ever knew. An interesting concept, as long as you don’t pick it up expecting a dystopian.<br /><br /><i>I received this book from the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. All quotes have been taken from the ARC which may have changed at the time of publishing. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12388811252209504972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_765104720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/765104720" />
    <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love"><img alt="nick (the infinite limits of love)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606193187p2/2993271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/765104720?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nick (the infinite limits of love)" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love">nick (the infinite limits of love)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer765104720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6410226594386279509"><br/>After the End is a book that everyone should go into without reading the blurb because it will take you by surprise and consequently, your reading experience will be much more entertaining. That's what I did and having not loved Amy Plum's Revenent series, I was very much surprised by how much I ended up enjoying this title.<br/><br/>The book is told in the dual POV of Juneau and Miles. While I did have issues with Miles' POV because of his personality, the dual POV in this book was essential to see the t</span>
  <span id="freeText6410226594386279509" style="display:none"><br />After the End is a book that everyone should go into without reading the blurb because it will take you by surprise and consequently, your reading experience will be much more entertaining. That's what I did and having not loved Amy Plum's Revenent series, I was very much surprised by how much I ended up enjoying this title.<br /><br />The book is told in the dual POV of Juneau and Miles. While I did have issues with Miles' POV because of his personality, the dual POV in this book was essential to see the two sides of the story. Juneau was by far my favorite of the two characters. She is someone who is easy to sympathize with. She finds out out of nowhere that her entire life has been a big lie and has to proceed to find her kidnapped clan. Juneau's calmness and maturity when it came to the obstacles that she was facing made her a likeable character, in my opinion. She refused to panic and did what she had to find her loved ones. I also really felt for her. I can't imagine what I would do if I was told that my entire life had been a joke, but Juneau handled everything with a level-head. My reason for not enjoying Miles initially was his motive. I got where he was coming from, but that didn't mean I didn't want to lash out at him every time he even thought of betraying Juneau. It did, however, like that the author had the two main characters mistrust each other for a very long time. Not only was it a refreshing feat in a YA book, but it was also realistic. As a result, the romance was very slow to develop and not a prevalent element.<br /><br />The plot is where I think the book needed a little work in. In all honesty, After the End felt for the most part like a long introduction. The world building was definitely up to par. We learn a lot about Juneau's life with her tribe in Alaska and a little about the mindset of the leader. I also really liked the inclusion of the supernatural element, the Yara, in the book. It was fascinating and by the end of the book, I was still itching to know more. The actual story, however, is just one long car chase with Juneau and Miles trying to escape people who are looking for them. I know this can be a turn off for many readers, but I found myself being thoroughly entertained throughout. I enjoyed the thrill of the chase. It helped that Amy Plum's writing was engrossing and had me hooked throughout. All I wanted to do was to keep reading on and on,so you can imagine the intense disappointment and frustration I felt when the book ended out of nowhere on an awful cliffhanger that made me want to scream.<br /><br />Ultimately, I thought After the End was a captivating book with a memorable heroine, an intriguing world and an engrossing writing style. I'm curious to see where the series is headed to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6410226594386279509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_828610814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/828610814" />
    <a title="paula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1543634-paula"><img alt="paula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1221836651p2/1543634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/828610814?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="paula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="paula" href="/user/show/1543634-paula">paula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1543634-paula?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1543634-paula?shelf=read-for-publication">read-for-publication</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828610814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15999444906296468197">Gr 6-12 -- When is an apocalypse not an apocalypse? When it’s a lie told to an isolated community living off the land. Juneau has grown up off the grid in a hunter-gatherer colony at the base of Denali Mountain in Alaska, convinced that she and her clan are the last civilized survivors of World War Three. But as she is out hunting one day, she sees a helicopter, and, returning to camp as quickly as she can, finds her entire clan, including her mentor, the powerful Whit, missing.<br/><br/>Juneau’s clan is </span>
  <span id="freeText15999444906296468197" style="display:none">Gr 6-12 -- When is an apocalypse not an apocalypse? When it’s a lie told to an isolated community living off the land. Juneau has grown up off the grid in a hunter-gatherer colony at the base of Denali Mountain in Alaska, convinced that she and her clan are the last civilized survivors of World War Three. But as she is out hunting one day, she sees a helicopter, and, returning to camp as quickly as she can, finds her entire clan, including her mentor, the powerful Whit, missing.<br /><br />Juneau’s clan is notable not only for their survivalist lifestyle, but for their mystical connection with a natural force called the Yara which allows them to perceive events at a distance, the past, and even the future. Juneau is particularly gifted in her ability to access the Yara, and her efforts to locate and rescue her clan are complicated by two separate factions who are pursuing her.<br /><br />Told in short chapters that alternate between Juneau’s point of view and that of the skeptical Miles, son of a pharmaceutical executive who will stop at nothing to acquire Juneau, After the End is a fast-paced adventure novel with some magic and romance - and one humdinger of a cliffhanger ending.<br /><br />I mean, it's fine. It's fine - if you accept that Mt McKinley is SO remote that a community could live there for 30 years and never see an airplane pass overhead. It's fine, if you are cool with someone seeing "a mountain range" "in the distance" and then running for about an hour and getting to the mountain. <br /><br />And for PETE'S SAKE, it's FINE, as long as you are ok with her first look at Anchorage: she travels by dogsled three days from McKinley towards the ocean, and comes out "on a ridge," from whence she can not only see the ocean, but also this thriving city, including people coming and going from businesses and their cars. <br /><br />I'm trying to picture this, a vantage point from which you can see an entire medium-sized city. If it were a small town, ok. If it were a town at the base of a cliff, like Boulder? But still! Even Boulder's not going to creep up on you like that. You can see all of Omaha from the ridge above the stockyards, but you wouldn't be able to see PEOPLE moving around. I went on Google Earth just to see if there was some unpopulated peak or ridge outside of Anchorage and aaaaggghhh you are saying I put too much thought into this stuff but COME ONNNNN! Does none of it matter? Can you just write whatever and as long as the characters are good-looking and the story's entertaining it's ok?<br /><br />Fuck it. It's Saturday night, I am up to date on my deadlines, I am shutting the laptop so I can watch Hansel and Gretel: Witch Hunters with my son.<br /><br />Adapted from my review for Booklist online</span>

<div id="review_949795673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/949795673" />
    <a title="Jessica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7227854-jessica"><img alt="Jessica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474169082p2/7227854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/949795673?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica " href="/user/show/7227854-jessica">Jessica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062225603" href="/book/show/18635064-after-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7227854-jessica?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer949795673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18177642817768613344">So I know I have a zillion other books that I should be reading and finishing but I was just craving a dystopian/post apocalyptic novel. AFTER THE END isn’t exactly either of those books but I am still so glad that I read it. When I picked up this book and started to read it I was thisclose to quitting on it. I was 5% in and I was bored, too many characters were being thrown at me and I wasn’t into it. My gut told me to stick with it and I’m happy I did because this book was really good! Juneau </span>
  <span id="freeText18177642817768613344" style="display:none">So I know I have a zillion other books that I should be reading and finishing but I was just craving a dystopian/post apocalyptic novel. AFTER THE END isn’t exactly either of those books but I am still so glad that I read it. When I picked up this book and started to read it I was thisclose to quitting on it. I was 5% in and I was bored, too many characters were being thrown at me and I wasn’t into it. My gut told me to stick with it and I’m happy I did because this book was really good! Juneau has believed the world outside her small clan in Alaska is a waste land, that WWIII has completely demolished what was left of our nation. When her family is kidnapped she takes a journey outside the clans bounds to save them but by doing so she is met with a surprise. The world has kept going. There was no World War 3, her clan has lied to her, the world she thought didn’t exist anymore has been there all along. It’s her mission to find her family, to find out who and why they were taken and how they, her clan, could lie to her for 17 years. Along the way she uses the power of the Yara to help guide her and on her journey she meets a young man named Miles. Let me tell you, Miles is a GIFT! I absolutely love, love, love his character, way more than I love Juneau. He is funny, witty, sarcastic and just a national treasure. He makes the entire book. I mean I would enjoy this story if it was just Juneau’s journey of finding her family, the truth, and trying to keep up with modern technology but Miles is what takes this book to the next level. I don’t really know how I feel about Juneau. I find her interesting but I think she’s kind of dull and uptight. I get why, she has a lot of responsibility and a weight on her shoulders, but at times I think, “Wow this girl needs to get a personality.”<br /><br />I do want to talk about the first 5% of this book. What I didn’t like about the beginning of the story was two things. 1.) Too many characters were being introduced in such a short amount of time and literally 75% of those characters were never mentioned again. Plum could have saved me the stress of trying to memorize 24 names and their connection to the main character. 2.) We only get a chapter or two of what life is like in the clan. I think I would have liked to have a little more insight into their life. That way when the clans memories were kidnapped I’d care a little more – if that makes sense.<br /><br />Right now I’m half way through book two UNTIL THE BEGINNING so be on the look out for another review on how things turn out for Juneau and Miles!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18177642817768613344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review949795673">

<div id="review_931770552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931770552" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931770552?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931770552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14936186955082390983">Rating: 3.5 Stars<br/><br/>I really, <i>really</i> enjoyed <i>After the End.</i> It isn't a dystopian novel--though the protagonist believes she's living in a post-apocalyptic world--and that premises is so wholly unique that it was enough to drag me through the alternating chapters in the beginning (which didn't do much for the plot) and into the rest of the enticing novel. Plum's latest series is written impeccably, putting into the confused mindset of our protagonist and introducing us to the culture shock of the mo</span>
  <span id="freeText14936186955082390983" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5 Stars<br /><br />I really, <i>really</i> enjoyed <i>After the End.</i> It isn't a dystopian novel--though the protagonist believes she's living in a post-apocalyptic world--and that premises is so wholly unique that it was enough to drag me through the alternating chapters in the beginning (which didn't do much for the plot) and into the rest of the enticing novel. Plum's latest series is written impeccably, putting into the confused mindset of our protagonist and introducing us to the culture shock of the modern world. In the midst of all this, though, the real plot lies in a chase, an adventure, and an uncovering of the secrets we're all dying to figure out. <br /><br />One of the strongest aspects of this novel is the relationship between Juneau and Mike, the main characters. For one, neither Juneau nor Mike see eye-to-eye on anything. Mike believes that Juneau has been brainwashed and struggles to believe the truth about her existence--that she was brought up in the wilderness of Alaska, living as a nomad for all her life. Similarly, Juneau cannot believe that her family and mentor lied to her and that, in truth, WWIII never occurred and that the modern world is safe and well. While Juneau is on a mission to find her family, who have been captured and moved across the country, Mike is there to bring Juneau to his father, the CEO of a major pharmaceutical company who believes that Juneau knows the ingredients to a secret drug being brewed in Alaska. Their rocky start and eventual friendship is an adventure to behold and I loved the slow and careful characterization of these two. <br /><br />I did struggle, though, with the actual genrefication of this novel. It started out dystopian, proceeded to be contemporary fiction, but truly ended with traces of paranormal and/or fantasy elements which, for a reader who likes to know what she's getting into, inspired a great deal of confusion. And that, sadly, dampened my enjoyment of this story. I really didn't know what to make of it and, to a large extent, still don't know what to make of the multiple genres this novel can fit into at different stages in its storyline. It was jarring and unexpected, to say the least, but I suspect I'll enjoy the sequel much more having this solid foundation going in. All in all, <i>After the End</i> was an unexpected surprise and I'm eager to devour its sequel soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14936186955082390983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_15927598'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15927598-a-matter-of-days"><img alt="A Matter of Days" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1347585360l/15927598._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eCMh2j4v95RSwVX4sQax2klQyYOBdaiAvLM7Jn7I7kIY6T1oeFA+XNBRmLUqfWVlDHStiIglZFIF7fPRBE0X0w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a5cBd0Q1TB6NJb2qKlXAszIRyqK0eH3YeP1RBbY/BRYLXR3FAkqF1g+1cOexLhQMdzWuqb0osQrBo5nyzLr8hw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3353516.Amy_Plum">About Amy Plum</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3353516.Amy_Plum"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1302475830p3/3353516.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3353516.Amy_Plum">Amy Plum

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3455988105382968136">Amy Plum is the international bestselling author of the DIE FOR ME series (Indie Next List pick, Romance Times top pick, and recipient of a starred review from School Library Journal). The books have been translated into thirteen foreign languages. The trilogy is accompanied by two eNovellas entitled DIE FOR HER and DIE ONCE MORE and a compendium entitled INSIDE THE WORLD OF DIE FOR ME. <br/><br/>In DREAMFA</span>
  <span id="freeText3455988105382968136" style="display:none">Amy Plum is the international bestselling author of the DIE FOR ME series (Indie Next List pick, Romance Times top pick, and recipient of a starred review from School Library Journal). The books have been translated into thirteen foreign languages. The trilogy is accompanied by two eNovellas entitled DIE FOR HER and DIE ONCE MORE and a compendium entitled INSIDE THE WORLD OF DIE FOR ME. <br /><br />In DREAMFALL and NEVERWAKE a radical experiment to cure chronic insomnia goes wrong, and its seven teenage test subjects are plunged into a shared coma populated by one another’s nightmares; those who die in the dream will also die in real life.<br /><br />Amy's action/adventure/magic duology, AFTER THE END and UNTIL THE BEGINNING, received starred reviews from Publishers Weekly, 4 1/2 stars from RT Book Reviews, and enthusiastic reviews from Kirkus, USA Today, ALA Booklist and School Library Journal.<br /><br />After being raised in Birmingham, Alabama, in a rather restrictive environment, AMY PLUM escaped to Chicago to an even more restrictive environment at a university that expelled people for dancing. (And where she was called to the dean’s office for “wearing too much black”.) After all of that restrictiveness, she was forced to run far far away, specifically to Paris, France, where she only wore black and danced all she wanted.<br /><br />After five years in Paris, she ventured to London, where she got an M.A. in Medieval Art History, specializing in Early Sienese Painting (1260-1348) mainly because it promised almost no hope of finding a paying job afterward.<br /><br />Amy managed to find work in the world of art and antiques in New York. But after almost a decade of high-pressure lifestyle in the Big Apple, she swapped her American city for a French village of 1300 inhabitants.<br /><br />After signing with HarperCollins for the DIE FOR ME series, Amy left her job as an English professor at Tours University to write full-time. She now lives in Paris with her two kids and her black lab, Oberon.<br /><br />She is a huge fan of Edward Gorey and Maira Kalman (and collects both of their books/art), as well as David Sedaris, Amadeo Modigliani, and Ira Glass.<br /><br />Check out videos and extras from Amy at <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/revenantcentral" rel="nofollow noopener">Revenant Central</a>.</span>
